<p>"<b>All About That Bass</b>" is the debut single by American singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Trainor" title="Meghan Trainor">Meghan Trainor</a>. Released by <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a> on June 30, 2014, it was recorded for her <a href="/wiki/Title_(EP)" title="Title (EP)">2014 debut EP</a> and her <a href="/wiki/Title_(Meghan_Trainor_album)" title="Title (Meghan Trainor album)">2015 studio album</a>, both named <i>Title</i>. Trainor co-wrote "All About That Bass" with its producer <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kadish" title="Kevin Kadish">Kevin Kadish</a>; it is a <a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_pop" title="Bubblegum pop">bubblegum pop</a>/<a href="/wiki/Doo-wop" title="Doo-wop">doo-wop</a> and retro-<a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> song that draws influences from various musical genres including <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>. Lyrically, it discusses positive <a href="/wiki/Body_image" title="Body image">body image</a>.</p>
<p>Several publications included it among the best songs of 2014 and received <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">Song of the Year</a>. It spent eight weeks atop the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and topped the charts in other twenty countries, including Canada, New Zealand, Switzerland and the United Kingdom. The song sold 11 million units worldwide, becoming the third best-selling song of 2014 and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling singles</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fatima_Robinson" title="Fatima Robinson">Fatima Robinson</a> directed the song's accompanying music video, a viral online success that was noted for its visuals and lighthearted nature. The song inspired a variety of <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral videos</a> and tributes, while <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i> recognized it as part of "the era of the big booty."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Complex_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Complex-5">[5]</a></sup> Trainor has performed it on television and at various concerts, and notable artists have recorded cover versions. Trainor regularly performed the song during her 2015 concert tours, the <a href="/wiki/That_Bass_Tour" title="That Bass Tour">That Bass Tour</a> and the <a href="/wiki/MTrain_Tour" title="MTrain Tour">MTrain Tour</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_and_development">Writing and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=All_About_That_Bass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Writing and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Developed in September 2013 by Trainor and American songwriter and producer <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kadish" title="Kevin Kadish">Kevin Kadish</a>, "All About That Bass" was written in 40 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Interview_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Interview-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Interview_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Interview-7">[7]</a></sup> At the time the song was written, Trainor lacked a recording contract but was writing tracks for other artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cosmo_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cosmo-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup> Kadish recalled the session as "a blind date" and felt they had a strong chemistry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-10">[10]</a></sup> The pair wrote the song with the intention of handing it to another recording artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Interview_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Interview-7">[7]</a></sup> Kadish then proposed the song title "All Bass, No Treble"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Interview_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Interview-6">[6]</a></sup> to Trainor who,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_2_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_2-11">[11]</a></sup> at the time, was in a phase of saying "I'm all about that Mexican food." She then responded to Kadish with the track's <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a>, "I'm all about that bass, no treble".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_Interview_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_Interview-12">[12]</a></sup> Suggesting the topics "booty" and thickness for the song, Trainor got inspiration from the size difference between the bottom and top sections of a <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">bass guitar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_2_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_2-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trainor and Kadish discussed their love for <a href="/wiki/1950s_in_music" title="1950s in music">1950s music</a>, and decided to incorporate the style into the song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Doo-wop" title="Doo-wop">doo-wop</a> because Trainor felt that the genre was very catchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jim_Farber_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_Farber-13">[13]</a></sup> Kadish then developed a modern <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beat</a> for the song and Trainor began <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_rap" title="Freestyle rap">freestyling</a> the first verse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup> She felt encouraged by the result and pictured the song to contain a theme of <a href="/wiki/Girl_power" title="Girl power">girl power</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_Interview_2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW_Interview_2-14">[14]</a></sup> Trainor intended for the song's lyrics to be about self-acceptance of body type, a theme inspired by her own struggles in self-image as a teenager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_2_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_2-11">[11]</a></sup> Kadish related to Trainor's lyric ideas due to his own experiences with weight insecurities during adolescence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Interview_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Interview-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_3_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_3-15">[15]</a></sup> Trainor wanted the track to criticize the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photoshop" title="Photoshop">photoshopped</a> images after she saw a feature on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i> of a model whose photographs were graphically edited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_2_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_2-11">[11]</a></sup> She obtained additional inspiration for the song from American singer <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Just_the_Way_You_Are_(Bruno_Mars_song)" title="Just the Way You Are (Bruno Mars song)">Just the Way You Are</a>" (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sullivan_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sullivan-16">[16]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Chordettes" title="The Chordettes">The Chordettes</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Lollipop_(1958_song)" title="Lollipop (1958 song)">Lollipop</a>" (1958).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farber_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farber-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=All_About_That_Bass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L.A._Reid.jpg"><img alt="An image of L.A. Reid dressed in a black suit." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="781" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/L.A._Reid.jpg/170px-L.A._Reid.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/L.A._Reid.jpg/255px-L.A._Reid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/L.A._Reid.jpg/340px-L.A._Reid.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L.A._Reid.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a> tagged "All About That Bass" as Trainor's debut single and decided that her <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> should remain as the track's final version with additional <a href="/wiki/Audio_mastering" title="Audio mastering">mastering</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While Trainor and Kadish were happy with the song after it was finished, they doubted its commercial prospects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feminism_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-Feminism-9">[9]</a></sup> They pitched the song to a variety of recording labels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DS_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-DS-18">[18]</a></sup> but all of them were critical that the track did not have more mainstream appeal and the production team did not make use of a <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Auto-Tune" title="Auto-Tune">Auto-Tune</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_3_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_3-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popjustice_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Popjustice-19">[19]</a></sup> The song was further criticized for not having a "big chorus", a suggestion that Trainor and Kadish balked at.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Interview_2_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Interview_2-11">[11]</a></sup> With no one else interested in recording it, Trainor agreed to use the song as her own at Kadish's suggestion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beast_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beast-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trainor recorded a <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> of the song and later met Paul Pontius—the <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> for <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a>—and sang the track for him. Even though admittedly nervous, she next sang it for Reid while accompanying herself on the <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Interview_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Interview-6">[6]</a></sup> After signing Trainor to Epic, Reid made a decision the final cut would be the same version as the demo but with additional <a href="/wiki/Audio_mastering" title="Audio mastering">mastering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_Interview_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_Interview-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popjustice_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Popjustice-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>"All About That Bass" was recorded at The Carriage House in <a href="/wiki/Nolensville,_Tennessee" title="Nolensville, Tennessee">Nolensville, Tennessee</a>. Trainor's vocals were recorded by Kadish, who was also responsible for the track's <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing_(recorded_music)" title="Audio mixing (recorded music)">mixing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Programming_(music)" title="Programming (music)">programming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sound_design" title="Sound design">sound design</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_engineering" title="Audio engineering">engineering</a>. The song's <a href="/wiki/Instrumentation_(music)" title="Instrumentation (music)">instrumentation</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">electric guitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bass_(instrument)" title="Bass (instrument)">bass</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a> by Kadish; and <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxophone" title="Saxophone">saxophone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hammond_organ" title="Hammond organ">Hammond organ</a> by <a href="/wiki/David_Baron_(composer)" title="David Baron (composer)">David Baron</a>. Trainor provided the track's <a href="/wiki/Clapping" title="Clapping">clapping</a> and additional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Percussion" title="Percussion">percussion</a>. The song was mastered by David Kutch at The Mastering Palace, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=All_About_That_Bass&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">

<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="18" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="All_About_That_Bass_by_Meghan_Trainor_(sample).ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
